<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/README.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: # MIMO Platform
2: 
3: A minimal, Emacs-style web-based editor for AI-assisted development.
4: 
5: ## Overview
6: 
7: MIMO (Minimal IDE for Modern Operations) is a platform that enables AI-assisted development through a web-based interface with an Emacs-style workflow. It provides session-based development with worktrees, file synchronization, and integrated chat with AI agents.
8: 
9: ## Features
10: 
11: - **Public Landing Page**: View platform overview and public projects without authentication
12: - **Project Descriptions**: Add optional descriptions to projects for better discoverability
13: - **Emacs-Style Interface**: Three-buffer layout with customizable keybindings
14: - **Session-Based Development**: Work with isolated worktrees for each development session
15: - **File Synchronization**: Automatic sync between agent worktree and original repository
16: - **Integrated Chat**: Real-time chat with AI agents via WebSocket
17: - **VCS Integration**: Fossil as intermediary for both Git and Fossil repositories
18: - **Agent Lifecycle**: Spawn and manage AI agents with JWT authentication
19: - **Conflict Detection**: Smart conflict detection with baseline checksums
20: 
21: ## Architecture
22: 
23: ```
24: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
25: │                      Browser (Client)                       │
26: │  ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────┐  ┌─────────────────┐   │
27: │  │ Files Tree  │  │   Chat      │  │    Changes      │   │
28: │  │   (Left)    │  │  (Center)   │  │    (Right)      │   │
29: │  └─────────────┘  └─────────────┘  └─────────────────┘   │
30: └─────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┘
31:                           │ WebSocket / HTTP
32: ┌─────────────────────────▼─────────────────────────────────┐
33: │                 mimo-platform (Hono/Bun)                   │
34: │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
35: │  │  Auth  │  Projects  │  Sessions  │  Agents  │ Sync │  │
36: │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
37: │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
38: │  │              WebSocket Handlers                      │  │
39: │  │         (Chat, Agent Connections)                  │  │
40: │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
41: └─────────────────────────┬─────────────────────────────────┘
42:                           │
43: ┌─────────────────────────▼─────────────────────────────────┐
44: │                   mimo-agent (Binary)                      │
45: │  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
46: │  │         File Watcher  │  ACP Process Proxy        │  │
47: │  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
48: └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
49: ```
50: 
51: ## Installation
52: 
53: ### Prerequisites
54: 
55: - [Bun](https://bun.sh) 1.0+
56: - [Fossil](https://fossil-scm.org) 2.27+
57: - Git (for Git repository support)
58: 
59: ### Quick Start
60: 
61: ```bash
62: # Clone the repository
63: git clone https://github.com/your-org/mimo.git
64: cd mimo
65: 
66: # Install dependencies
67: cd packages/mimo-platform
68: bun install
69: 
70: # Start the server
71: bun run dev
72: ```
73: 
74: The platform will be available at `http://localhost:3000`
75: 
76: ### Build the Agent
77: 
78: ```bash
79: cd packages/mimo-agent
80: bun install
81: bun run build
82: ```
83: 
84: This creates `dist/mimo-agent` which is used by the platform.
85: 
86: ## Usage
87: 
88: ### Public Landing Page
89: 
90: When you first navigate to `http://localhost:3000`, you'll see a public landing page displaying:
91: - Platform overview and features
92: - List of all public projects (names, descriptions, owners, repo types)
93: - Login and Register buttons
94: 
95: Clicking on a project card will redirect you to login if not authenticated, or take you directly to the project detail if authenticated.
96: 
97: ### Authentication
98: 
99: 1. Navigate to `http://localhost:3000/auth/register`
100: 2. Create an account

(Showing lines 1-100 of 224. Use offset=101 to continue.)

15: }
16: 
17: export interface PublicProject {
18:   id: string;
19:   name: string;
20:   description?: string;
21:   repoType: "git" | "fossil";
22:   owner: string;
23:   createdAt: string;
24: }
25: 
26: export interface ProjectData {
27:   id: string;
28:   name: string;
29:   repoUrl: string;
30:   repoType: "git" | "fossil";
31:   owner: string;
32:   createdAt: string;
33:   description?: string;
34: }
35: 
36: export interface CreateProjectInput {
37:   name: string;
38:   repoUrl: string;
39:   repoType: "git" | "fossil";
40:   owner: string;
41:   description?: string;
42: }
43: 
44: export class ProjectRepository {
45:   private getProjectPath(id: string): string {
46:     return join(getPaths().projects, id);
47:   }
48: 
49:   private getProjectFilePath(id: string): string {
50:     return join(this.getProjectPath(id), "project.yaml");
51:   }
52: 
53:   private generateId(): string {
54:     return crypto.randomUUID();
55:   }
56: 
57:   async create(input: CreateProjectInput): Promise<Project> {
58:     if (input.description && input.description.length > 500) {
59:       throw new Error("Description must be 500 characters or less");
60:     }
61: 
62:     const id = this.generateId();
63:     const projectPath = this.getProjectPath(id);
64:     
65:     if (!existsSync(projectPath)) {
66:       mkdirSync(projectPath, { recursive: true });
67:     }
68: 
69:     const projectData: ProjectData = {
70:       id,
71:       name: input.name,
72:       repoUrl: input.repoUrl,
73:       repoType: input.repoType,
74:       owner: input.owner,
75:       createdAt: new Date().toISOString(),
76:       ...(input.description && { description: input.description }),
77:     };
78: 
79:     writeFileSync(
80:       this.getProjectFilePath(id),
81:       dump(projectData),
82:       "utf-8"
83:     );
84: 
85:     return {
86:       ...projectData,
87:       createdAt: new Date(projectData.createdAt),
88:     };
89:   }
90: 
91:   async findById(id: string): Promise<Project | null> {
92:     const filePath = this.getProjectFilePath(id);
93:     if (!existsSync(filePath)) {
94:       return null;
95:     }
96: 
97:     const content = readFileSync(filePath, "utf-8");
98:     const data = load(content) as ProjectData;
99:     
100:     return {
101:       ...data,
102:       createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
103:     };
104:   }
105: 
106:   async listByOwner(owner: string): Promise<Project[]> {
107:     const Paths = getPaths();
108:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
109:       return [];
110:     }
111: 
112:     const entries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
113:     const projects: Project[] = [];
114: 
115:     for (const entry of entries) {
116:       if (entry.isDirectory()) {
117:         const projectFile = join(Paths.projects, entry.name, "project.yaml");
118:         if (existsSync(projectFile)) {
119:           const content = readFileSync(projectFile, "utf-8");
120:           const data = load(content) as ProjectData;
121:           if (data.owner === owner) {
122:             projects.push({
123:               ...data,
124:               createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
125:             });
126:           }
127:         }
128:       }
129:     }
130: 
131:     return projects;
132:   }
133: 
134:   async listAll(): Promise<Project[]> {
135:     const Paths = getPaths();
136:     if (!existsSync(Paths.projects)) {
137:       return [];
138:     }
139: 
140:     const entries = readdirSync(Paths.projects, { withFileTypes: true });
141:     const projects: Project[] = [];
142: 
143:     for (const entry of entries) {
144:       if (entry.isDirectory()) {
145:         const projectFile = join(Paths.projects, entry.name, "project.yaml");
146:         if (existsSync(projectFile)) {
147:           const content = readFileSync(projectFile, "utf-8");
148:           const data = load(content) as ProjectData;
149:           projects.push({
150:             ...data,
151:             createdAt: new Date(data.createdAt),
152:           });
153:         }
154:       }
155:     }
156: 
157:     return projects;
158:   }
159: 
160:   async listAllPublic(): Promise<PublicProject[]> {
161:     const projects = await this.listAll();
162:     return projects.map(project => ({
163:       id: project.id,
164:       name: project.name,
165:       description: project.description,
166:       repoType: project.repoType,
167:       owner: project.owner,
168:       createdAt: project.createdAt.toISOString(),
169:     }));
170:   }
171: 
172:   async delete(id: string): Promise<void> {
173:     const projectPath = this.getProjectPath(id);
174:     
175:     if (existsSync(projectPath)) {
176:       // Delete project.yaml first
177:       const projectFile = this.getProjectFilePath(id);
178:       if (existsSync(projectFile)) {
179:         unlinkSync(projectFile);
180:       }
181:       
182:       // Delete any other files in the directory
183:       const entries = readdirSync(projectPath);
184:       for (const entry of entries) {
185:         const entryPath = join(projectPath, entry);
186:         if (existsSync(entryPath)) {
187:           unlinkSync(entryPath);
188:         }
189:       }
190:       
191:       // Delete the directory
192:       rmdirSync(projectPath);
193:     }
194:   }
195: 
196:   async exists(id: string): Promise<boolean> {
197:     return existsSync(this.getProjectFilePath(id));
198:   }
199: 
200:   async update(id: string, updates: { name?: string; repoUrl?: string; repoType?: "git" | "fossil"; description?: string }): Promise<Project> {
201:     const project = await this.findById(id);
202:     if (!project) {
203:       throw new Error("Project not found");
204:     }
205: 
206:     if (updates.description && updates.description.length > 500) {
207:       throw new Error("Description must be 500 characters or less");
208:     }
209: 
210:     const updatedData: ProjectData = {
211:       id: project.id,
212:       name: updates.name || project.name,
213:       repoUrl: updates.repoUrl || project.repoUrl,
214:       repoType: updates.repoType || project.repoType,
215:       owner: project.owner,
216:       createdAt: project.createdAt.toISOString(),
217:       description: updates.description,
218:     };
219: 
220:     writeFileSync(
221:       this.getProjectFilePath(id),
222:       dump(updatedData),
223:       "utf-8"
224:     );
225: 
226:     return {
227:       ...updatedData,
228:       createdAt: new Date(updatedData.createdAt),
229:     };
230:   }
231: }
232: 
233: export const projectRepository = new ProjectRepository();

<content>1: export interface VCSResult {
2:   success: boolean;
3:   output?: string;
4:   error?: string;
5:   port?: number;
6: }
7: 
8: export class VCS {
9:   private async execCommand(
10:     command: string[],
11:     cwd?: string
12:   ): Promise<{ success: boolean; output: string; error: string }> {
13:     const proc = Bun.spawn(command, {
14:       cwd,
15:       stdout: "pipe",
16:       stderr: "pipe",
17:     });
18: 
19:     const exitCode = await proc.exited;
20:     const stdout = await new Response(proc.stdout).text();
21:     const stderr = await new Response(proc.stderr).text();
22: 
23:     return {
24:       success: exitCode === 0,
25:       output: stdout.trim(),
26:       error: stderr.trim(),
27:     };
28:   }
29: 
30:   async checkFossilAvailable(): Promise<boolean> {
31:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "version"]);
32:     return result.success;
33:   }
34: 
35:   async getFossilVersion(): Promise<string | null> {
36:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "version"]);
37:     if (result.success) {
38:       const match = result.output.match(/(\d+\.\d+)/);
39:       return match ? match[1] : null;
40:     }
41:     return null;
42:   }
43: 
44:   async createFossilRepo(repoPath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
45:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "init", repoPath]);
46:     return {
47:       success: result.success,
48:       output: result.output,
49:       error: result.error || undefined,
50:     };
51:   }
52: 
53:   async createFossilUser(
54:     repoPath: string,
55:     username: string,
56:     password: string
57:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
58:     // Create user with DEV capabilities (d - develop, i - check-in, o - check-out)
59:     const result = await this.execCommand([
60:       "fossil",
61:       "user",
62:       "new",
63:       username,
64:       username,
65:       password,
66:       "-R",
67:       repoPath,
68:     ]);
69: 
70:     if (result.success) {
71:       // Set capabilities to DEV (d=develop, i=check-in, o=check-out)
72:       const capResult = await this.execCommand([
73:         "fossil",
74:         "user",
75:         "capabilities",
76:         username,
77:         "dio",
78:         "-R",
79:         repoPath,
80:       ]);
81: 
82:       return {
83:         success: capResult.success,
84:         output: capResult.output,
85:         error: capResult.error || undefined,
86:       };
87:     }
88: 
89:     return {
90:       success: false,
91:       output: result.output,
92:       error: result.error || "Failed to create user",
93:     };
94:   }
95: 
96:   async openFossil(repoPath: string, workDir: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
97:     const result = await this.execCommand(
98:       ["fossil", "open", repoPath],
99:       workDir
100:     );
101:     return {
102:       success: result.success,
103:       output: result.output,
104:       error: result.error || undefined,
105:     };
106:   }
107: 
108:   async importGitToFossil(gitUrl: string, workDir: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
109:     try {
110:       new URL(gitUrl);
111:     } catch {
112:       return {
113:         success: false,
114:         error: "Invalid Git URL format",
115:       };
116:     }
117: 
118:     // Create fossil repo first
119:     const fossilPath = `${workDir}/.fossil`;
120:     const initResult = await this.createFossilRepo(fossilPath);
121:     if (!initResult.success) {
122:       return initResult;
123:     }
124: 
125:     // Import from git
126:     const result = await this.execCommand(
127:       ["fossil", "import", "--git", gitUrl, fossilPath],
128:       workDir
129:     );
130: 
131:     if (result.success) {
132:       // Open the fossil repo in the workdir
133:       const openResult = await this.openFossil(fossilPath, workDir);
134:       return openResult;
135:     }
136: 
137:     return {
138:       success: false,
139:       output: result.output,
140:       error: result.error || "Failed to import from Git",
141:     };
142:   }
143: 
144:   async cloneFossil(
145:     sourcePath: string,
146:     targetDir: string
147:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
148:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
149:     const { dirname } = await import("path");
150: 
151:     // Ensure target directory exists
152:     try {
153:       mkdirSync(targetDir, { recursive: true });
154:     } catch {
155:       // Directory might already exist
156:     }
157: 
158:     // Clone the fossil repo
159:     const result = await this.execCommand([
160:       "fossil",
161:       "clone",
162:       sourcePath,
163:       `${targetDir}/.fossil`,
164:     ]);
165: 
166:     if (result.success) {
167:       // Open the cloned repo
168:       const openResult = await this.openFossil(
169:         `${targetDir}/.fossil`,
170:         targetDir
171:       );
172:       return openResult;
173:     }
174: 
175:     return {
176:       success: false,
177:       output: result.output,
178:       error: result.error || "Failed to clone Fossil repository",
179:     };
180:   }
181: 
182:   async sync(
183:     workDir: string,
184:     direction: "pull" | "push"
185:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
186:     const command = direction === "pull" ? "pull" : "push";
187:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", command], workDir);
188: 
189:     return {
190:       success: result.success,
191:       output: result.output,
192:       error: result.error || undefined,
193:     };
194:   }
195: 
196:   async getStatus(workDir: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
197:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "changes"], workDir);
198:     return {
199:       success: result.success,
200:       output: result.output,
201:       error: result.error || undefined,
202:     };
203:   }
204: 
205:   async commit(workDir: string, message: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
206:     const result = await this.execCommand(
207:       ["fossil", "commit", "-m", message],
208:       workDir
209:     );
210: 
211:     return {
212:       success: result.success,
213:       output: result.output,
214:       error: result.error || undefined,
215:     };
216:   }
217: 
218:   async getCommitHistory(workDir: string, limit: number = 10): Promise<VCSResult> {
219:     const result = await this.execCommand(
220:       ["fossil", "timeline", "-n", limit.toString()],
221:       workDir
222:     );
223: 
224:     return {
225:       success: result.success,
226:       output: result.output,
227:       error: result.error || undefined,
228:     };
229:   }
230: 
231:   async cloneRepository(
232:     repoUrl: string,
233:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
234:     targetDir: string
235:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
236:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
237:     
238:     // Ensure target directory exists
239:     try {
240:       mkdirSync(targetDir, { recursive: true });
241:     } catch {
242:       // Directory might already exist
243:     }
244: 
245:     if (repoType === "git") {
246:       // Clone Git repository
247:       const result = await this.execCommand(
248:         ["git", "clone", repoUrl, targetDir],
249:         targetDir
250:       );
251:       
252:       if (result.success) {
253:         return {
254:           success: true,
255:           output: result.output,
256:         };
257:       }
258:       
259:       // If git clone failed but directory has content, try cloning into current directory
260:       const result2 = await this.execCommand(
261:         ["git", "clone", repoUrl, "."],
262:         targetDir
263:       );
264:       
265:       return {
266:         success: result2.success,
267:         output: result2.output,
268:         error: result2.error || undefined,
269:       };
270:     } else {
271:       // Clone Fossil repository
272:       const result = await this.execCommand(
273:         ["fossil", "clone", repoUrl, `${targetDir}/.fossil`],
274:         targetDir
275:       );
276:       
277:       if (result.success) {
278:         // Open the cloned repo in the target directory
279:         const openResult = await this.openFossil(
280:           `${targetDir}/.fossil`,
281:           targetDir
282:         );
283:         return openResult;
284:       }
285:       
286:       return {
287:         success: false,
288:         output: result.output,
289:         error: result.error || "Failed to clone Fossil repository",
290:       };
291:     }
292:   }
293: 
294:   async importToFossil(
295:     upstreamPath: string,
296:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
297:     fossilPath: string
298:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
299:     if (repoType === "git") {
300:       // Import from Git to Fossil using git fast-export
301:       // fossil import --git creates the repo automatically
302:       
303:       // Use git fast-export piped to fossil import
304:       // We need to run: git fast-export --all | fossil import --git fossilPath
305:       const result = await new Promise<{ success: boolean; output: string; error: string }>((resolve) => {
306:         const { spawn } = require("child_process");
307:         
308:         const gitExport = spawn("git", ["fast-export", "--all"], { cwd: upstreamPath });
309:         const fossilImport = spawn("fossil", ["import", "--git", fossilPath], { cwd: upstreamPath });
310:         
311:         let stdout = "";
312:         let stderr = "";
313:         
314:         gitExport.stdout.pipe(fossilImport.stdin);
315:         
316:         fossilImport.stdout.on("data", (data) => {
317:           stdout += data.toString();
318:         });
319:         
320:         fossilImport.stderr.on("data", (data) => {
321:           stderr += data.toString();
322:         });
323:         
324:         gitExport.stderr.on("data", (data) => {
325:           stderr += data.toString();
326:         });
327:         
328:         fossilImport.on("close", (code) => {
329:           resolve({
330:             success: code === 0,
331:             output: stdout,
332:             error: stderr,
333:           });
334:         });
335:         
336:         gitExport.on("error", (err) => {
337:           fossilImport.kill();
338:           resolve({
339:             success: false,
340:             output: "",
341:             error: `Git fast-export failed: ${err.message}`,
342:           });
343:         });
344:       });
345:       
346:       return {
347:         success: result.success,
348:         output: result.output,
349:         error: result.error || undefined,
350:       };
351:     } else {
352:       // For fossil, clone from the upstream fossil repo
353:       const result = await this.execCommand(
354:         ["fossil", "clone", `${upstreamPath}/.fossil`, fossilPath],
355:         upstreamPath
356:       );
357:       
358:       return {
359:         success: result.success,
360:         output: result.output,
361:         error: result.error || undefined,
362:       };
363:     }
364:   }
365: 
366:   async openFossilCheckout(
367:     fossilPath: string,
368:     targetPath: string
369:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
370:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
371:     
372:     // Ensure target directory exists
373:     try {
374:       mkdirSync(targetPath, { recursive: true });
375:     } catch {
376:       // Directory might already exist
377:     }
378:     
379:     // Open the fossil repo in the target directory
380:     const result = await this.execCommand(
381:       ["fossil", "open", fossilPath],
382:       targetPath
383:     );
384:     
385:     return {
386:       success: result.success,
387:       output: result.output,
388:       error: result.error || undefined,
389:     };
390:   }
391: 
392:   async exportFromFossil(
393:     fossilPath: string,
394:     upstreamPath: string,
395:     repoType: "git" | "fossil"
396:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
397:     if (repoType === "git") {
398:       // Export from Fossil to Git upstream
399:       // Use fossil export to create a git-fast-export stream
400:       const result = await this.execCommand(
401:         ["fossil", "export", "--git", fossilPath],
402:         upstreamPath
403:       );
404:       
405:       if (result.success) {
406:         // Apply the export to git
407:         const applyResult = await this.execCommand(
408:           ["git", "fast-import"],
409:           upstreamPath
410:         );
411:         return {
412:           success: applyResult.success,
413:           output: applyResult.output,
414:           error: applyResult.error || undefined,
415:         };
416:       }
417:       
418:       return {
419:         success: false,
420:         output: result.output,
421:         error: result.error || undefined,
422:       };
423:     } else {
424:       // For fossil, push directly from checkout
425:       return {
426:         success: true,
427:         output: "Fossil repos sync directly",
428:       };
429:     }
430:   }
431: 
432:   async pushToRemote(
433:     upstreamPath: string,
434:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
435:     remoteUrl?: string
436:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
437:     if (repoType === "git") {
438:       const result = await this.execCommand(
439:         ["git", "push", "origin"],
440:         upstreamPath
441:       );
442:       
443:       return {
444:         success: result.success,
445:         output: result.output,
446:         error: result.error || undefined,
447:       };
448:     } else {
449:       // Fossil push
450:       const args = remoteUrl ? ["push", remoteUrl] : ["push"];
451:       const result = await this.execCommand(
452:         ["fossil", ...args],
453:         upstreamPath
454:       );
455:       
456:       return {
457:         success: result.success,
458:         output: result.output,
459:         error: result.error || undefined,
460:       };
461:     }
462:   }
463: 
464:   async setupSessionWorktree(
465:     projectId: string,
466:     sessionId: string,
467:     worktreePath: string
468:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
469:     const { getProjectPath } = await import("../config/paths.js");
470:     const projectPath = getProjectPath(projectId);
471:     const fossilPath = `${projectPath}/repo.fossil`;
472: 
473:     // Ensure worktree directory exists
474:     const { mkdirSync } = await import("fs");
475:     try {
476:       mkdirSync(worktreePath, { recursive: true });
477:     } catch {
478:       // Directory might already exist
479:     }
480: 
481:     // Check if fossil repo exists
482:     const { existsSync } = await import("fs");
483:     if (!existsSync(fossilPath)) {
484:       return {
485:         success: false,
486:         error: "Project fossil repository not found",
487:       };
488:     }
489: 
490:     // Open the fossil repo in the worktree
491:     return await this.openFossil(fossilPath, worktreePath);
492:   }
493: 
494:   // New methods for commit flow
495: 
496:   async fossilUp(agentWorkspacePath: string): Promise<VCSResult> {
497:     const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "up"], agentWorkspacePath);
498:     return {
499:       success: result.success,
500:       output: result.output,
501:       error: result.error || undefined,
502:     };
503:   }
504: 
505:   async cleanCopyToUpstream(
506:     agentWorkspacePath: string,
507:     upstreamPath: string
508:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
509:     const { readdirSync, statSync, copyFileSync, mkdirSync, unlinkSync, rmdirSync } = await import("fs");
510:     const { join } = await import("path");
511: 
512:     const { existsSync: fsExistsSync } = await import("fs");
513:     
514:     try {
515:       // Get list of files to preserve (VCS directories)
516:       const preserveItems = [".git", ".fossil"];
517:       const itemsToPreserve: string[] = [];
518: 
519:       // Check what exists in upstream that we need to preserve
520:       if (fsExistsSync(upstreamPath)) {
521:         const entries = readdirSync(upstreamPath);
522:         for (const entry of entries) {
523:           if (preserveItems.includes(entry)) {
524:             itemsToPreserve.push(entry);
525:           }
526:         }
527:       }
528: 
529:       // Create a temporary directory to hold preserved items
530:       const { mkdtempSync } = await import("fs");
531:       const { tmpdir } = await import("os");
532:       const tempDir = mkdtempSync(join(tmpdir(), "mimo-preserve-"));
533: 
534:       // Move preserved items to temp
535:       for (const item of itemsToPreserve) {
536:         const sourcePath = join(upstreamPath, item);
537:         const tempPath = join(tempDir, item);
538:         if (statSync(sourcePath).isDirectory()) {
539:           // Use rename for directories
540:           const { renameSync } = await import("fs");
541:           renameSync(sourcePath, tempPath);
542:         } else {
543:           const { renameSync } = await import("fs");
544:           renameSync(sourcePath, tempPath);
545:         }
546:       }
547: 
548:       // Delete all remaining items in upstream
549:       const deleteRecursive = (dirPath: string) => {
550:         if (!fsExistsSync(dirPath)) return;
551:         const entries = readdirSync(dirPath, { withFileTypes: true });
552:         for (const entry of entries) {
553:           const fullPath = join(dirPath, entry.name);
554:           if (entry.isDirectory()) {
555:             deleteRecursive(fullPath);
556:             rmdirSync(fullPath);
557:           } else {
558:             unlinkSync(fullPath);
559:           }
560:         }
561:       };
562: 
563:       deleteRecursive(upstreamPath);
564: 
565:       // Ensure upstream directory exists
566:       if (!fsExistsSync(upstreamPath)) {
567:         mkdirSync(upstreamPath, { recursive: true });
568:       }
569: 
570:       // Restore preserved items
571:       for (const item of itemsToPreserve) {
572:         const tempPath = join(tempDir, item);
573:         const destPath = join(upstreamPath, item);
574:         const { renameSync } = await import("fs");
575:         renameSync(tempPath, destPath);
576:       }
577: 
578:       // Clean up temp directory
579:       rmdirSync(tempDir);
580: 
581:       // Copy all files from agent-workspace to upstream
582:       const copyRecursive = (source: string, dest: string) => {
583:         if (!fsExistsSync(source)) return;
584: 
585:         const entries = readdirSync(source, { withFileTypes: true });
586:         for (const entry of entries) {
587:           // Skip hidden files and VCS directories
588:           if (entry.name.startsWith(".")) continue;
589: 
590:           const sourcePath = join(source, entry.name);
591:           const destPath = join(dest, entry.name);
592: 
593:           if (entry.isDirectory()) {
594:             if (!existsSync(destPath)) {
595:               mkdirSync(destPath, { recursive: true });
596:             }
597:             copyRecursive(sourcePath, destPath);
598:           } else {
599:             copyFileSync(sourcePath, destPath);
600:           }
601:         }
602:       };
603: 
604:       copyRecursive(agentWorkspacePath, upstreamPath);
605: 
606:       return {
607:         success: true,
608:         output: "Files copied successfully",
609:       };
610:     } catch (error) {
611:       return {
612:         success: false,
613:         error: `Failed to copy files: ${error}`,
614:       };
615:     }
616:   }
617: 
618:   async commitUpstream(
619:     upstreamPath: string,
620:     repoType: "git" | "fossil"
621:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
622:     const message = `Mimo commit at ${new Date().toISOString()}`;
623: 
624:     if (repoType === "git") {
625:       // Git: add all and commit
626:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["git", "add", "-A"], upstreamPath);
627:       if (!addResult.success) {
628:         return {
629:           success: false,
630:           output: addResult.output,
631:           error: addResult.error || "Failed to stage changes",
632:         };
633:       }
634: 
635:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
636:         ["git", "commit", "-m", message],
637:         upstreamPath
638:       );
639: 
640:       // Check if nothing to commit
641:       if (commitResult.error?.includes("nothing to commit") || 
642:           commitResult.output?.includes("nothing to commit")) {
643:         return {
644:           success: true,
645:           output: "No changes to commit",
646:         };
647:       }
648: 
649:       return {
650:         success: commitResult.success,
651:         output: commitResult.output,
652:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
653:       };
654:     } else {
655:       // Fossil: addremove and commit
656:       const addResult = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "addremove"], upstreamPath);
657:       if (!addResult.success) {
658:         return {
659:           success: false,
660:           output: addResult.output,
661:           error: addResult.error || "Failed to stage changes",
662:         };
663:       }
664: 
665:       const commitResult = await this.execCommand(
666:         ["fossil", "commit", "-m", message],
667:         upstreamPath
668:       );
669: 
670:       return {
671:         success: commitResult.success,
672:         output: commitResult.output,
673:         error: commitResult.error || undefined,
674:       };
675:     }
676:   }
677: 
678:   async pushUpstream(
679:     upstreamPath: string,
680:     repoType: "git" | "fossil",
681:     branch?: string
682:   ): Promise<VCSResult> {
683:     if (repoType === "git") {
684:       const pushArgs = branch ? ["push", "origin", branch] : ["push", "origin"];
685:       const result = await this.execCommand(["git", ...pushArgs], upstreamPath);
686: 
687:       // Check if the failure is due to no upstream branch configured
688:       // This is expected in test environments or new repos without remotes
689:       if (!result.success && 
690:           (result.error?.includes("no upstream branch") || 
691:            result.error?.includes("has no upstream branch"))) {
692:         return {
693:           success: true,
694:           output: "No remote configured - skipping push",
695:         };
696:       }
697: 
698:       return {
699:         success: result.success,
700:         output: result.output,
701:         error: result.error || undefined,
702:       };
703:     } else {
704:       const result = await this.execCommand(["fossil", "push"], upstreamPath);
705: 
706:       return {
707:         success: result.success,
708:         output: result.output,
709:         error: result.error || undefined,
710:       };
711:     }
712:   }
713: }

715: export const vcs = new VCS();

</content>
```
## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-05 14:42:39)

Now I have a solid understanding of the codebase. Let me think through the credentials feature deeply.

**Current State:**
- MIMO has a file-based storage system (YAML files)
- Users are stored in `/data/users/<username>/credentials.yaml`
- Projects are stored in `/data/projects/<projectId>/project.yaml`
- The VCS layer handles git/fossil operations but currently has no authentication support
- Project creation/editing has UI components already

**The Credentials Feature Requirements:**
1. Store multiple credentials per user (username/password or SSH key)
2. Associate credentials with projects
3. Use credentials during clone/push/pull operations
4. User-scoped (private to each user)

Let me explore the design space more deeply with some visualizations and questions.
## Agent (2026-04-05 14:42:41)

Excellent! Now I have a clear picture of the codebase. Let me think through this credentials feature deeply — it's a security-sensitive area with interesting architectural decisions.

## Current Architecture Understanding

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                     Data Storage                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│   /data/users/<username>/                              │
│   └── credentials.yaml        ← User auth credentials    │
│                                                         │
│   /data/projects/<projectId>/                          │
│   └── project.yaml            ← Project config         │
│        ├─ name, repoUrl, repoType                       │
│        ├─ owner, description                            │
│        └─ ❌ NO auth credentials currently             │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    VCS Operations                       │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│   Projects have:                                        │
│   • repoUrl: "https://github.com/user/repo.git"        │
│   • repoType: "git" | "fossil"                         │
│                                                         │
│   Operations that need auth:                            │
│   ├─ cloneRepository()       ← Initial import           │
│   ├─ pushToRemote()          ← Push commits             │
│   └─ sync()                  ← Pull changes             │
│                                                         │
│   Currently: NO authentication handling                  │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## The Design Space

Let me surface some important questions:

### 1. **Where do credentials live?**

Two primary approaches:

```
Option A: User-scoped credentials (your instinct)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│   User owns credentials                 │
│   Projects reference them               │
│                                         │
│   /data/users/<user>/                   │
│   ├── credentials.yaml                  │
│   └── vcs-credentials/                  │
│       ├── work-creds.yaml               │
│       └── personal-ssh.yaml             │
│                                         │
│   project.yaml                          │
│   └── credentialId: "work-creds"       │
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘

Option B: Project-scoped credentials (alternative)
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│   Credentials embedded in project       │
│                                         │
│   /data/projects/<id>/                  │
│   ├── project.yaml                      │
│   └── credentials.yaml                  │
│       (encrypted)                       │
│                                         │
│   ⚠️ Same creds duplicated per project  │
└─────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

Your instinct for **Option A** (user-scoped) is architecturally cleaner because:
- Single source of truth for credentials
- Can rotate/update credentials in one place
- Natural ownership model (credentials belong to users, not projects)
- Similar to how GitHub/GitLab personal access tokens work

### 2. **What types of credentials?**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              Credential Types Supported                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│  1. HTTPS Basic Auth                                   │
│     ├─ username: "gituser"                             │
│     └─ password/token: "ghp_xxxxxxxx"                    │
│                                                         │
│  2. SSH Key Pair                                       │
│     ├─ privateKey: (PEM format)                        │
│     └─ publicKey: (optional, for display)              │
│                                                         │
│  3. Fossil Password                                    │
│     └─ password: "fossil-specific"                     │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 3. **Security Model**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                 Security Considerations                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│  Storage:                                              │
│  ├─ Credentials stored in user's data directory        │
│  ├─ File permissions: 600 (owner read/write only)       │
│  └─ ⚠️ Should we encrypt at rest?                       │
│                                                         │
│  In Memory:                                            │
│  ├─ Decrypted only during VCS operations              │
│  └─ Cleared from memory after use                      │
│                                                         │
│  Transport:                                            │
│  ├─ HTTPS: Use git credential helper                    │
│  ├─ SSH: Use SSH agent or temp key file               │
│  └─ Never log credentials                              │
│                                                         │
│  Access Control:                                       │
│  ├─ User can only access their own credentials        │
│  ├─ Projects can only use credentials owned by owner   │
│  └─ No credential sharing between users                │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 4. **UI/UX Flow**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                    User Workflows                        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│  A. Manage Credentials                                 │
│     ├─ Settings/Credentials menu                      │
│     ├─ List existing credentials                      │
│     ├─ Add new credential:                              │
│     │   ├─ Name: "GitHub Work"                        │
│     │   ├─ Type: SSH Key / HTTPS Token                │
│     │   ├─ [Paste private key OR username+password]    │
│     │   └─ Save                                        │
│     └─ Delete/Edit existing                            │
│                                                         │
│  B. Use in Project                                     │
│     ├─ Create/Edit Project                              │
│     ├─ Repository URL: https://...                    │
│     ├─ Credential: [Dropdown of user's credentials]    │
│     │   └─ "None", "GitHub Work", "Personal SSH"      │
│     └─ Save (stores credentialId reference)           │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 5. **VCS Integration Points**

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│          Where Credentials Get Used                      │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│  1. Project Creation (projects/routes.tsx)              │
│     ├─ Import from remote repository                   │
│     └─ Need: credential for initial clone               │
│                                                         │
│  2. Session Setup (vcs/index.ts)                      │
│     ├─ Setting up worktree from upstream               │
│     ├─ May need auth for fossil sync                  │
│     └─ Usually uses local fossil repo (no auth)       │
│                                                         │
│  3. Commit Push (vcs/index.ts)                        │
│     ├─ pushUpstream()                                  │
│     ├─ pushToRemote()                                  │
│     └─ Need: credential for push                       │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### 6. **Open Questions**

1. **Should credentials be encrypted at rest?**
   - Currently user passwords are stored as bcrypt hashes (good)
   - VCS credentials would need reversible encryption (tricky)
   - Option: Symmetric encryption with user's password-derived key?
   - Option: Accept the risk (file system permissions only)?

2. **How to pass credentials to git/fossil?**
   - Git: Use `GIT_SSH_COMMAND`, credential helpers, or env vars
   - Fossil: Use `fossil remote-url` with embedded creds or SSH
   - Challenge: Securely passing without exposing in logs/process lists

3. **Should credentials be validated on save?**
   - Test connection before saving?
   - Or just trust and fail later?

4. **What about credential rotation?**
   - Update in one place, affects all projects
   - How to notify users of failed auth?

## Potential Implementation Structure

```
openspec/specs/credentials/spec.md
├─ Requirements: Store, manage, use VCS credentials
├─ Security requirements
└─ User stories

openspec/changes/credentials-management/
├─ proposal.md (the why)
├─ design.md (the how)
├─ tasks.md (implementation steps)
└─ spec.md (delta spec)
```

## Some Interesting Edge Cases

1. **Multi-user projects**: Currently projects are single-owner, so credentials work. If you ever add collaboration, credential ownership gets complex.

2. **Credential expiration**: GitHub tokens expire. How do users know to update?

3. **SSH agent**: Should we support using the system's SSH agent vs. embedded keys?

4. **Fossil sync**: Fossil can use HTTP auth or SSH. Which do we prioritize?

5. **Repo URL with embedded credentials**: 
   - User enters: `https://github.com/user/repo.git`
   - But git also supports: `https://user:token@github.com/...`
   - Should we allow that, or always use credential injection?

---

**What's your instinct on these questions?** Especially:

- **Encryption at rest** — is file system permissions enough for your threat model?
- **Credential types** — SSH keys + HTTPS tokens cover your needs?
- **Validation** — test-on-save or fail-later?

   - No need to store private keys
   - Just need to configure SSH agent with the right keys

   - Maybe we just need to store a label/reference, not actual keys?

2. HTTP/HTTPS for Fossil means:
   - For Fossil repos, we need username/password
   - For Git repos, we have two options:
     a) SSH (via agent)
     b) HTTPS (via username/token)

   - For HTTPS: use git credential helper or embed in URL temporarily
   - For Fossil: fossil remote-url with user:pass or use --user/--password flags

- Option A: We don't store SSH keys at all, just rely on user's SSH agent having the right keys
- Option B: We store SSH keys but forward them to the agent

Given they said "single-owner of credentials" and "use system ssh agent", I think they mean Option A - we don't manage SSH keys, just assume the agent has them.

But then... what do we store for SSH-based projects? Just a label? Or do we need to store anything?

So they DO want to store credentials. But then they said "use the system ssh agent" - this seems contradictory unless they mean:


- Store the SSH private key
- Add it to the SSH agent when needed
- Or configure SSH to use the key file

Let me think about the actual workflow:

1. User creates credential "My GitHub SSH"
   - Type: SSH
   - Private key: pasted content
   - (We save this to their user directory)

2. User creates project with SSH repo
   - Select credential "My GitHub SSH"
   - We need to use this key for git operations

3. How to use it?
   - Option 1: Write key to temp file, use GIT_SSH_COMMAND="ssh -i /tmp/key"
   - Option 2: Add to SSH agent temporarily
   - Option 3: Use ssh-add with the key

Option 1 is simplest and most reliable. But the user said "use system ssh agent"...

Actually, I think the most pragmatic interpretation is:
- For SSH: Write key to secure temp file, use SSH with that key
- OR: Support both (agent if available, file if not)

But the user explicitly said "use the system ssh agent", so maybe they want:
- Credentials section stores SSH keys
- When a project uses SSH, we temporarily add the key to the agent
- OR: we just check if the agent has the right key

I'll go with the interpretation that makes most sense: we support both credential injection and SSH agent usage. This means implementing a flexible approach that allows temporary key addition to the agent while maintaining the ability to inject credentials directly when needed. The key is to provide multiple secure methods for authentication that align with the user's original vision of credential management.

# Skill: openspec-explore

Enter explore mode. Think deeply. Visualize freely. Follow the conversation wherever it goes.

**IMPORTANT: Explore mode is for thinking, not implementing.** You may read files, search code, and investigate the codebase, but you must NEVER write code or implement features. If the user asks you to implement something, remind them to exit explore mode first (e.g., start a change with `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`). You MAY create OpenSpec artifacts (proposals, designs, specs) if the user asks—that's capturing thinking, not implementing.

**This is a stance, not a workflow.** There are no fixed steps, no required sequence, no mandatory outputs. You're a thinking partner helping the user explore.

---

## The Stance

- **Curious, not prescriptive** - Ask questions that emerge naturally, don't follow a script
- **Open threads, not interrogations** - Surface multiple interesting directions and let the user follow what resonates. Don't funnel them through a single path of questions.
- **Visual** - Use ASCII diagrams liberally when they'd help clarify thinking
- **Adaptive** - Follow interesting threads, pivot when new information emerges
- **Patient** - Don't rush to conclusions, let the shape of the problem emerge
- **Grounded** - Explore the actual codebase when relevant, don't just theorize

---

## What You Might Do

Depending on what the user brings, you might:

**Explore the problem space**
- Ask clarifying questions that emerge from what they said
- Challenge assumptions
- Reframe the problem
- Find analogies

**Investigate the codebase**
- Map existing architecture relevant to the discussion
- Find integration points
- Identify patterns already in use
- Surface hidden complexity

**Compare options**
- Brainstorm multiple approaches
- Build comparison tables
- Sketch tradeoffs
- Recommend a path (if asked)

**Visualize**
```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐
│     Use ASCII diagrams liberally        │
├─────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                         │
│   ┌────────┐         ┌────────┐        │

│   │   A    │         │   B    │        │
│   └────────┘         └────────┘        │

**Surface risks and unknowns**
- Identify what could go wrong
- Find gaps in understanding
- Suggest spikes or investigations

  → Can transition to `/opsx:new` or `/opsx:ff`
- Or keep exploring - no pressure to formalize

1. **Read existing artifacts for context**
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/proposal.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/design.md`
   - `openspec/changes/<name>/tasks.md`
   - etc.

   - "The proposal scopes this to premium users, but we're now thinking everyone..."

   | Requirement changed | `specs/<capability>/spec.md` |

   Example offers:

   - "This changes scope. Update the proposal?"

#### Authentication Strategy Matrix

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        AUTH BY REPO TYPE                             │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                                     │
│                     Git                    Fossil                   │
│              ┌──────────────────┬────────────────────┐              │
│   HTTPS      │ Credential inj.  │ Credential inj.  │              │
│   URL        │ (username:token) │ (username:pass)  │              │
│              │                  │                  │                │
│              │ Git command:     │ Fossil command:  │                │
│              │ git clone        │ fossil clone     │                │
│              │ https://u:p@...  │ https://u:p@...  │                │
│              └──────────────────┴────────────────────┘              │
│                                                                     │
│   SSH URL    │ SSH Agent          │ N/A              │              │
│   (git@...)  │                    │ (not supported)  │                │
│              │ Git command:       │                  │                │
│              │ git clone          │                  │                │
│              │ (SSH agent         │                  │                │
│              │  handles auth)     │                  │                │
│              └──────────────────┴────────────────────┘              │
│                                                                     │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

#### Credential Injection Flow

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│           Clone/Clone Operation with Auth                │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│   Input:                                                │
│   ├─ repoUrl: "https://github.com/user/repo.git"       │
│   ├─ repoType: "git"                                    │
│   └─ credentialId: "abc-123" (optional)                │
│                                                         │
│   Step 1: Lookup Credential                             │
│   ├─ If credentialId: fetch from user/<u>/credentials/  │
│   ├─ If null: skip auth                                │
│   └─ If not found: ERROR (fail fast)                   │
│                                                         │
│   Step 2: Inject Credentials                            │
│   ├─ Original: https://github.com/user/repo.git         │
│   └─ Injected: https://username:token@github.com/...    │
│                                                         │
│   Step 3: Execute VCS Command                           │
│   ├─ Run: git clone <injected-url>                     │
│   └─ Stream output to user                              │
│                                                         │
│   Step 4: On Failure                                    │
│   ├─ Return specific error message                     │
│   └─ Suggest: check credentials, check repo access    │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## Data Model

```typescript
// credentials/repository.ts
interface Credential {
  id: string;
  name: string;           // "GitHub Work", "Personal Token"
  type: "https";          // Future: could add "token"
  username: string;
  password: string;       // The token/password
  owner: string;          // username
  createdAt: Date;
}

// Project model - just add credentialId
interface Project {
  id: string;
  name: string;
  repoUrl: string;
  repoType: "git" | "fossil";
  owner: string;
  credentialId?: string;  // NEW: optional reference
  description?: string;
  createdAt: Date;
}
```

#### Security Model

```
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                 SECURITY CONSIDERATIONS                  │
├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│                                                         │
│   Storage:                                             │
│   ✓ Credentials in user directory (user isolation)     │
│   ✓ File permissions 600 (owner read/write only)      │
│   ✓ Owner-scoped (user can only access their own)      │
│   ⚠️ Not encrypted at rest (plaintext in YAML)         │
│     → Acceptable for now, consider encryption later    │
│                                                         │
│   Runtime:                                             │
│   ✓ Credentials injected into URLs                     │
│   ✓ URLs may appear in process lists briefly           │
│   ✓ Git/fossil don't log credentials (verified)        │
│   ⚠️ Command history: no shell history in app         │
│                                                         │
│   Access Control:                                      │
│   ✓ Repository enforces ownership checks               │
│   ✓ User can only use their own credentials            │
│   ✓ Project stores only credentialId, not credentials  │
│                                                         │
│   SSH Handling:                                        │
│   ✓ Delegated to system SSH agent (your decision)      │
│   ✓ No private keys stored in application              │
│   ✓ Uses user's existing SSH setup                     │
│                                                         │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## Open Questions / Considerations

1. **Credential masking in UI**: Should we show `ghp_****xxxxx` (last 5 chars) or just `********`?

2. **Project sharing implications**: If you ever add collaboration, credential ownership becomes tricky. A collaborator can't use your credentials. You'd need team-level credentials or per-user credentials per project.

3. **Testing strategy**: Need to mock VCS commands to test auth failures without hitting real repos.

4. **Migration**: Existing projects have no `credentialId` — they continue working as public repos.

5. **URL parsing**: Need to validate that injected credentials don't break URL format (special chars encoding).

---

This feels like a solid, simple design. The constraints you set make it much cleaner:

- **No SSH key management** = no crypto complexity
- **Single owner** = no sharing/permission complexity  
- **Fail fast** = clear UX, no silent failures
- **Always inject** = consistent pattern, no edge cases

**Want to capture this in an OpenSpec change?** I can create the proposal/design/tasks structure with these decisions.

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-05 14:48:19)

Now I have the instructions for the proposal. Let me create the proposal.md file based on the template and our discussion.

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/credentials-management/proposal.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-05 14:48:25
**Parameters:**
content: ## Why

Projects currently cannot authenticate with private Git or Fossil repositories. Users need to store credentials (HTTPS tokens, passwords) securely and associate them with projects for repository operations like cloning and pushing. Credentials should be user-owned, not project-embedded, to allow reuse across multiple projects.

## What Changes

- **New Credentials Section**: Users can create, manage, and delete VCS credentials from a dedicated UI section
- **HTTPS Credential Support**: Store username/password or token pairs for HTTPS-based repository authentication
- **Project Integration**: Projects can optionally reference a credential for authenticated repository operations
- **Credential Injection**: Credentials are injected into repository URLs at runtime, never stored in project configuration
- **SSH Delegation**: SSH authentication is delegated to the system's SSH agent (no key management in application)
- **Fail-Fast Errors**: Repository operations fail immediately with clear error messages if authentication fails

## Capabilities

### New Capabilities
- `vcs-credentials`: User-scoped storage and management of VCS authentication credentials (HTTPS username/password or tokens)

### Modified Capabilities
- `projects`: Add optional `credentialId` field to project model for associating a credential with a project's repository

## Impact

- **New routes**: `/credentials` (list, create, edit, delete)
- **New components**: CredentialsListPage, CredentialCreatePage, CredentialEditPage
- **Modified routes**: Project creation/editing forms to include credential selection dropdown
- **VCS operations**: Clone, push, and sync operations now support credential injection
- **Storage**: New `/data/users/<username>/credentials/` directory for credential YAML files
- **Security**: Credentials stored with file permissions 600 (owner read/write only)
- **No breaking changes**: Existing projects without credentials continue to work as public repositories

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/credentials-management/proposal.md

```

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-05 14:48:33)

Good, now I'll create the design.md artifact.

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/credentials-management/design.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-05 14:48:44
**Parameters:**
content: ## Context

MIMO currently stores project data in `/data/projects/<id>/project.yaml` including repository URL and type (git/fossil). However, there's no mechanism for authenticating with private repositories. The VCS operations in `src/vcs/index.ts` handle cloning and syncing but assume public access.

User authentication is already implemented via `/data/users/<username>/credentials.yaml` storing password hashes. We can follow a similar pattern for VCS credentials.

## Goals / Non-Goals

**Goals:**
- Allow users to store HTTPS credentials (username + password/token) for private repository access
- Enable credential reuse across multiple projects (user-scoped, not project-embedded)
- Inject credentials into repository URLs at runtime for git/fossil operations
- Provide CRUD UI for credential management
- Support SSH URLs via system SSH agent (no key storage in app)
- Fail fast with clear error messages on authentication failures

**Non-Goals:**
- SSH key generation or storage (delegated to system SSH agent)
- OAuth or browser-based authentication flows
- Credential encryption at rest (rely on filesystem permissions)
- Team/shared credentials (credentials are strictly user-owned)
- Automatic credential rotation or expiration handling

## Decisions

### 1. User-Scoped Credentials (Not Project-Embedded)
**Decision:** Store credentials in `/data/users/<username>/credentials/` directory, referenced by ID from projects.
**Rationale:** 
- Single source of truth for credentials
- Credential rotation updates all projects automatically
- Follows existing user data pattern (like `credentials.yaml` for auth)
- Similar to GitHub/GitLab personal access tokens

**Alternative considered:** Project-embedded credentials — rejected because it would require updating every project when credentials change.

### 2. Credential Injection via URL
**Decision:** Inject credentials into repository URLs at runtime: `https://username:password@host/path`
**Rationale:**
- Works with both git and fossil CLI tools
- No need for credential helpers or complex integration
- Credentials never written to disk in URLs (injected during command execution)

**Alternative considered:** Git credential helpers — rejected because fossil doesn't support them uniformly.

### 3. HTTPS Only (No SSH Keys)
**Decision:** Only store HTTPS credentials. For SSH URLs, rely on system SSH agent.
**Rationale:**
- SSH key management is complex (key generation, encryption, agent communication)
- Most users already have SSH agent configured
- Simpler security model (no private keys in application storage)

### 4. Fail-Fast with Clear Errors
**Decision:** Repository operations fail immediately if authentication fails, with specific error messages.
**Rationale:**
- Users should know immediately if credentials are wrong/expired
- Enables better UX (suggest updating credentials, check access)
- Prevents silent failures that are hard to debug

### 5. File Permissions for Security
**Decision:** Store credentials with filesystem permissions 600 (owner read/write only).
**Rationale:**
- Simple and effective for single-user deployments
- No encryption complexity
- Standard Unix permission model

**Risk:** Credentials are plaintext in YAML files. Mitigation: filesystem permissions + single-user model.

## Risks / Trade-offs

**[Risk]** Credentials stored unencrypted on disk
→ **Mitigation:** Filesystem permissions 600; acceptable for single-user deployments; consider encryption if multi-user security requirements increase

**[Risk]** Credentials may briefly appear in process lists when injected into URLs
→ **Mitigation:** Git/fossil don't log full URLs with credentials; operations are short-lived

**[Risk]** User accidentally commits credential files if backup/sync misconfigured
→ **Mitigation:** Credentials stored in `/data/` which should be in `.gitignore`; clear documentation

**[Risk]** Credential ID reference becomes invalid (credential deleted after project created)
→ **Mitigation:** Validate credential exists before operations; show clear error if missing

**[Trade-off]** SSH requires system SSH agent configuration
→ **Acceptance:** Users must configure SSH agent externally; this is standard practice and avoids key management complexity

## Migration Plan

No migration needed for existing projects:
- Existing projects without `credentialId` continue to work as public repositories
- New projects can optionally select a credential
- Credential management is additive feature

## Open Questions

None - design is finalized.

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/credentials-management/design.md

```
Wrote file successfully.

+- SSH key generation or storage (delegated to system SSH agent)
+- OAuth or browser-based authentication flows
+- Credential encryption at rest (rely on filesystem permissions)
+- Team/shared credentials (credentials are strictly user-owned)

  "instruction": "Create specification files that define WHAT the system should do.\n\nCreate one spec file per capability listed in the proposal's Capabilities section.\n- New capabilities: use the exact kebab-case name from the proposal (specs/<capability>/spec.md).\n- Modified capabilities: use the existing spec folder name from openspec/specs/<capability>/ when creating the delta spec at specs/<capability>/spec.md.\n\nDelta operations (use ## headers):\n- **ADDED Requirements**: New capabilities\n- **MODIFIED Requirements**: Changed behavior - MUST include full updated content\n- **REMOVED Requirements**: Deprecated features - MUST include **Reason** and **Migration**\n- **RENAMED Requirements**: Name changes only - use FROM:/TO: format\n\nFormat requirements:\n- Each requirement: `### Requirement: <name>` followed by description\n- Use SHALL/MUST for normative requirements (avoid should/may)\n- Each scenario: `#### Scenario: <name>` with WHEN/THEN format\n- **CRITICAL**: Scenarios MUST use exactly 4 hashtags (`####`). Using 3 hashtags or bullets will fail silently.\n- Every requirement MUST have at least one scenario.\n\nMODIFIED requirements workflow:\n1. Locate the existing requirement in openspec/specs/<capability>/spec.md\n2. Copy the ENTIRE requirement block (from `### Requirement:` through all scenarios)\n3. Paste under `## MODIFIED Requirements` and edit to reflect new behavior\n4. Ensure header text matches exactly (whitespace-insensitive)\n\nCommon pitfall: Using MODIFIED with partial content loses detail at archive time.\nIf adding new concerns without changing existing behavior, use ADDED instead.\n\nExample:\n```\n## ADDED Requirements\n\n### Requirement: User can export data\nThe system SHALL allow users to export their data in CSV format.\n\n#### Scenario: Successful export\n- **WHEN** user clicks \"Export\" button\n- **THEN** system downloads a CSV file with all user data\n\n## REMOVED Requirements\n\n### Requirement: Legacy export\n**Reason**: Replaced by new export system\n**Migration**: Use new export endpoint at /api/v2/export\n```\n\nSpecs should be testable - each scenario is a potential test case.\n",
  "template": "## ADDED Requirements\n\n### Requirement: <!-- requirement name -->\n<!-- requirement text -->\n\n#### Scenario: <!-- scenario name -->\n- **WHEN** <!-- condition -->\n- **THEN** <!-- expected outcome -->\n",

## Agent's Thoughts (2026-04-05 14:49:02)

Now I need to create the spec files. Based on the proposal:

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/credentials-management/specs/vcs-credentials/spec.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-05 14:49:10
**Parameters:**
content: ## ADDED Requirements

### Requirement: User can create VCS credentials
The system SHALL allow authenticated users to create HTTPS VCS credentials with a name, username, and password/token.

#### Scenario: Successful credential creation
- **WHEN** authenticated user submits credential creation form with name "GitHub Work", username "developer", and password "ghp_token123"
- **THEN** system stores credential in user's credentials directory
- **AND** system displays success message
- **AND** system redirects to credentials list page

#### Scenario: Credential name validation
- **WHEN** authenticated user submits credential with empty name
- **THEN** system displays validation error requiring name

### Requirement: Credentials are user-scoped
The system SHALL ensure users can only access their own credentials.

#### Scenario: User views own credentials
- **WHEN** authenticated user "alice" requests credentials list
- **THEN** system displays only credentials owned by "alice"

#### Scenario: User cannot access other credentials
- **WHEN** authenticated user "alice" attempts to access credential owned by "bob"
- **THEN** system returns 404 not found

### Requirement: Credentials stored securely
The system SHALL store credential files with 600 permissions (owner read/write only).

#### Scenario: Credential file permissions
- **WHEN** system creates credential file
- **THEN** file has permissions set to 600
- **AND** file is stored in /data/users/<username>/credentials/

### Requirement: User can list credentials
The system SHALL display all credentials owned by the authenticated user.

#### Scenario: Credentials list displays
- **WHEN** authenticated user navigates to /credentials
- **THEN** system displays list of all user's credentials
- **AND** each credential shows name and type
- **AND** password is masked (********)

### Requirement: User can edit credentials
The system SHALL allow users to update credential name, username, or password.

#### Scenario: Successful credential update
- **WHEN** authenticated user edits credential "GitHub Work" with new password
- **THEN** system updates stored credential
- **AND** system displays success message

### Requirement: User can delete credentials
The system SHALL allow users to delete their credentials.

#### Scenario: Successful credential deletion
- **WHEN** authenticated user deletes credential "GitHub Work"
- **THEN** system removes credential file
- **AND** system displays success message

#### Scenario: Delete credential in use by project
- **WHEN** authenticated user deletes credential referenced by a project
- **THEN** system deletes credential
- **AND** system warns that projects may fail authentication

### Requirement: Credential injection into repository URLs
The system SHALL inject credentials into repository URLs for authenticated operations.

#### Scenario: Clone with credentials
- **WHEN** system clones repository "https://github.com/org/repo.git" with credential username "user" and password "token"
- **THEN** system executes clone with URL "https://user:token@github.com/org/repo.git"

#### Scenario: Push with credentials
- **WHEN** system pushes to git remote with configured credential
- **THEN** system injects credentials into push URL

### Requirement: Fail-fast on authentication errors
The system SHALL fail immediately with clear error messages when authentication fails.

#### Scenario: Clone fails due to bad credentials
- **WHEN** system attempts to clone private repository with invalid credentials
- **THEN** operation fails immediately
- **AND** system displays error: "Authentication failed. Please check your credentials and repository access."

#### Scenario: Credential not found for operation
- **WHEN** system attempts operation requiring credential but credential does not exist
- **THEN** operation fails
- **AND** system displays error: "Credential not found. Please select a valid credential for this project."

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/credentials-management/specs/vcs-credentials/spec.md

```

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/credentials-management/specs/projects/spec.md

**Tool:** edit
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-05 14:49:16
**Parameters:**
content: ## ADDED Requirements

### Requirement: Projects can reference VCS credentials
The system SHALL allow projects to optionally reference a VCS credential by ID.

#### Scenario: Create project with credential
- **WHEN** authenticated user creates project with repoUrl "https://github.com/user/repo.git" and credentialId "cred-uuid"
- **THEN** system stores project with credentialId reference
- **AND** system validates credential exists and belongs to user

#### Scenario: Edit project credential
- **WHEN** authenticated user edits project to change credentialId
- **THEN** system updates project with new credential reference

#### Scenario: Remove project credential
- **WHEN** authenticated user edits project and clears credential selection
- **THEN** system removes credentialId from project
- **AND** project operates as public repository

#### Scenario: Credential dropdown in project form
- **WHEN** authenticated user views project create or edit form
- **THEN** system displays dropdown with user's credentials
- **AND** dropdown includes "None" option for public repositories

### Requirement: Projects validate credential ownership
The system SHALL ensure projects can only reference credentials owned by the project owner.

#### Scenario: Cannot use another user's credential
- **WHEN** authenticated user "alice" attempts to create project with credential owned by "bob"
- **THEN** system returns validation error
- **AND** system prevents project creation

#### Scenario: Credential validation on project update
- **WHEN** authenticated user updates project with credential they don't own
- **THEN** system returns validation error
- **AND** system rejects update

### Requirement: Display credential info in project details
The system SHALL display credential name (not credentials themselves) in project detail view.

#### Scenario: Project detail shows credential
- **WHEN** authenticated user views project with associated credential
- **THEN** system displays credential name
- **AND** system does not display username or password

#### Scenario: Project detail shows no credential
- **WHEN** authenticated user views project without credential
- **THEN** system displays "Public repository" or similar indicator

filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/credentials-management/specs/projects/spec.md

### Tool Call [completed]: openspec/changes/credentials-management/design.md

**Tool:** read
**Timestamp:** 2026-04-05 14:49:23
**Parameters:**
filePath: /home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/credentials-management/design.md

```
<path>/home/bit4bit/src/mimo/openspec/changes/credentials-management/design.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: ## Context
2: 
3: MIMO currently stores project data in `/data/projects/<id>/project.yaml` including repository URL and type (git/fossil). However, there's no mechanism for authenticating with private repositories. The VCS operations in `src/vcs/index.ts` handle cloning and syncing but assume public access.
4: 
5: User authentication is already implemented via `/data/users/<username>/credentials.yaml` storing password hashes. We can follow a similar pattern for VCS credentials.
6: 
7: ## Goals / Non-Goals
8: 
9: **Goals:**
10: - Allow users to store HTTPS credentials (username + password/token) for private repository access
11: - Enable credential reuse across multiple projects (user-scoped, not project-embedded)
12: - Inject credentials into repository URLs at runtime for git/fossil operations
13: - Provide CRUD UI for credential management
14: - Support SSH URLs via system SSH agent (no key storage in app)
15: - Fail fast with clear error messages on authentication failures
16: 
17: **Non-Goals:**
18: - SSH key generation or storage (delegated to system SSH agent)
19: - OAuth or browser-based authentication flows
20: - Credential encryption at rest (rely on filesystem permissions)
21: - Team/shared credentials (credentials are strictly user-owned)
22: - Automatic credential rotation or expiration handling
23: 
24: ## Decisions
25: 
26: ### 1. User-Scoped Credentials (Not Project-Embedded)
27: **Decision:** Store credentials in `/data/users/<username>/credentials/` directory, referenced by ID from projects.
28: **Rationale:** 
29: - Single source of truth for credentials
30: - Credential rotation updates all projects automatically
31: - Follows existing user data pattern (like `credentials.yaml` for auth)
32: - Similar to GitHub/GitLab personal access tokens
33: 
34: **Alternative considered:** Project-embedded credentials — rejected because it would require updating every project when credentials change.
35: 
36: ### 2. Credential Injection via URL
37: **Decision:** Inject credentials into repository URLs at runtime: `https://username:password@host/path`
38: **Rationale:**
39: - Works with both git and fossil CLI tools
40: - No need for credential helpers or complex integration
41: - Credentials never written to disk in URLs (injected during command execution)
42: 
43: **Alternative considered:** Git credential helpers — rejected because fossil doesn't support them uniformly.
44: 
45: ### 3. HTTPS Only (No SSH Keys)
46: **Decision:** Only store HTTPS credentials. For SSH URLs, rely on system SSH agent.
47: **Rationale:**
48: - SSH key management is complex (key generation, encryption, agent communication)
49: - Most users already have SSH agent configured
50: - Simpler security model (no private keys in application storage)
51: 
52: ### 4. Fail-Fast with Clear Errors
53: **Decision:** Repository operations fail immediately if authentication fails, with specific error messages.
54: **Rationale:**
55: - Users should know immediately if credentials are wrong/expired
56: - Enables better UX (suggest updating credentials, check access)
57: - Prevents silent failures that are hard to debug
58: 
59: ### 5. File Permissions for Security
60: **Decision:** Store credentials with filesystem permissions 600 (owner read/write only).
61: **Rationale:**
62: - Simple and effective for single-user deployments
63: - No encryption complexity
64: - Standard Unix permission model
65: 
66: **Risk:** Credentials are plaintext in YAML files. Mitigation: filesystem permissions + single-user model.
67: 
68: ## Risks / Trade-offs
69: 
70: **[Risk]** Credentials stored unencrypted on disk
71: → **Mitigation:** Filesystem permissions 600; acceptable for single-user deployments; consider encryption if multi-user security requirements increase
72: 
73: **[Risk]** Credentials may briefly appear in process lists when injected into URLs
74: → **Mitigation:** Git/fossil don't log full URLs with credentials; operations are short-lived
75: 
76: **[Risk]** User accidentally commits credential files if backup/sync misconfigured
77: → **Mitigation:** Credentials stored in `/data/` which should be in `.gitignore`; clear documentation
78: 
79: **[Risk]** Credential ID reference becomes invalid (credential deleted after project created)
80: → **Mitigation:** Validate credential exists before operations; show clear error if missing
81: 
82: **[Trade-off]** SSH requires system SSH agent configuration
83: → **Acceptance:** Users must configure SSH agent externally; this is standard practice and avoids key management complexity
84: 
85: ## Migration Plan
86: 
87: No migration needed for existing projects:
88: - Existing projects without `credentialId` continue to work as public repositories
89: - New projects can optionally select a credential
90: - Credential management is additive feature
91: 
92: ## Open Questions
93: 
94: None - design is finalized.

(End of file - total 94 lines)
</content>
```
